<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Eukaryotic cell" redirects here. For the journal, see <a href="/wiki/Eukaryotic_Cell_(journal)" title="Eukaryotic Cell (journal)">Eukaryotic Cell (journal)</a>.</div>

<p>Eukaryotic organisms that cannot be classified under the kingdoms Plantae, Animalia or Fungi are sometimes grouped in the <a href="/wiki/Paraphyly" title="Paraphyly">paraphyly</a> <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protista" title="Protista">Protista</a></b>.
</p>
</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p><b>Eukaryotes</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">j</span><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ær/: 'arr' in 'marry'">ær</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>) are <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a> whose <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cells</a> have a <a href="/wiki/Cell_nucleus" title="Cell nucleus">nucleus</a> enclosed within a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_envelope" title="Nuclear envelope">nuclear envelope</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Youngson_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Youngson-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nelson&amp;Cox_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson&amp;Cox-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-3">[3]</a></sup> They belong to the group of organisms <b>Eukaryota</b> or <b>Eukarya</b>; their name comes from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%B5%E1%BD%96" title="wikt:εὖ">εὖ</a> (<i>eu</i>, "well" or "good") and <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%BA%CE%AC%CF%81%CF%85%CE%BF%CE%BD" title="wikt:κάρυον">κάρυον</a> (<i>karyon</i>, "nut" or "kernel").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OnlineEtDict_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-OnlineEtDict-4">[4]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Domain_(biology)" title="Domain (biology)">domain</a> Eukaryota makes up one of the <a href="/wiki/Three-domain_system" title="Three-domain system">three domains of life</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Archaea" title="Archaea">archaea</a> (both <a href="/wiki/Prokaryote" title="Prokaryote">prokaryotes</a>) make up the other two domains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gabaldón_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gabaldón-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-w1990_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-w1990-6">[6]</a></sup> The eukaryotes are usually now regarded as having emerged in the Archaea or as a sister of the <a href="/wiki/Asgard_(archaea)" title="Asgard (archaea)">Asgard</a> archaea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_2016_apr_11_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_2016_apr_11-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> This implies that there are only <a href="/wiki/Two-domain_system" title="Two-domain system">two domains of life</a>, Bacteria and Archaea, with eukaryotes incorporated among archaea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-10">[10]</a></sup> Eukaryotes represent a small minority of the number of organisms;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whitman_etal_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whitman_etal-11">[11]</a></sup> however, due to their generally much larger size, their collective global <a href="/wiki/Biomass_(ecology)" title="Biomass (ecology)">biomass</a> is estimated to be about equal to that of prokaryotes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whitman_etal_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Whitman_etal-11">[11]</a></sup> Eukaryotes emerged approximately 2.3–1.8 billion years ago, during the <a href="/wiki/Proterozoic" title="Proterozoic">Proterozoic</a> eon, likely as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagellated_cell" title="Flagellated cell">flagellated</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phagotroph" title="Phagotroph">phagotrophs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>Eukaryotic cells typically contain other <a href="/wiki/Organelle" title="Organelle">membrane-bound organelles</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrion" title="Mitochondrion">mitochondria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golgi_apparatus" title="Golgi apparatus">Golgi apparatus</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">chloroplasts</a> can be found in <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a>. Prokaryotic cells may contain <a href="/wiki/Organelle#Prokaryotic_organelles" title="Organelle">primitive organelles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Eukaryotes may be either <a href="/wiki/Unicellular_organism" title="Unicellular organism">unicellular</a> or <a href="/wiki/Multicellular_organism" title="Multicellular organism">multicellular</a>, and include many <a href="/wiki/Cell_type" title="Cell type">cell types</a> forming different kinds of <a href="/wiki/Tissue_(biology)" title="Tissue (biology)">tissue</a>; in comparison, prokaryotes are typically unicellular. <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">Animals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a> are the most familiar eukaryotes; other eukaryotes are sometimes called <a href="/wiki/Protist" title="Protist">protists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whittaker_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whittaker-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Eukaryotes can reproduce both <a href="/wiki/Asexual_reproduction" title="Asexual reproduction">asexually</a> through <a href="/wiki/Mitosis" title="Mitosis">mitosis</a> and sexually through <a href="/wiki/Meiosis" title="Meiosis">meiosis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gamete" title="Gamete">gamete</a> fusion. In mitosis, one cell divides to produce two genetically identical cells. In meiosis, <a href="/wiki/DNA_replication" title="DNA replication">DNA replication</a> is followed by two rounds of <a href="/wiki/Cell_division" title="Cell division">cell division</a> to produce four <a href="/wiki/Ploidy" title="Ploidy">haploid</a> daughter cells. These act as sex cells or gametes. Each gamete has just one set of chromosomes, each a unique mix of the corresponding pair of parental <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosomes</a> resulting from <a href="/wiki/Genetic_recombination" title="Genetic recombination">genetic recombination</a> during meiosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cell_features">Cell features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Cell features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="433" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="BC1_Cytology.webm" height="124" id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/BC1_Cytology.webm/220px--BC1_Cytology.webm.jpg" preload="none" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="1037216" data-framerate="30" data-height="480" data-shorttitle="VP9 480P" data-title="SD VP9 (480P)" data-transcodekey="480p.vp9.webm" data-width="854" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/0/01/BC1_Cytology.webm/BC1_Cytology.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; <p><a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)#Eukaryotic_cells" title="Cell (biology)">Eukaryotic cells</a> are typically much larger than those of <a href="/wiki/Prokaryote" title="Prokaryote">prokaryotes</a>, having a volume of around 10,000 times greater than the prokaryotic cell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> They have a variety of internal membrane-bound structures, called <a href="/wiki/Organelle" title="Organelle">organelles</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Cytoskeleton" title="Cytoskeleton">cytoskeleton</a> composed of <a href="/wiki/Microtubule" title="Microtubule">microtubules</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microfilament" title="Microfilament">microfilaments</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Intermediate_filament" title="Intermediate filament">intermediate filaments</a>, which play an important role in defining the cell's organization and shape. Eukaryotic <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> is divided into several linear bundles called <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosomes</a>, which are separated by a <a href="/wiki/Spindle_apparatus" title="Spindle apparatus">microtubular spindle</a> during nuclear division.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_membranes">Internal membranes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Internal membranes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Endomembrane_system_diagram_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="486" data-file-width="612" decoding="async" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Endomembrane_system_diagram_en.svg/260px-Endomembrane_system_diagram_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Endomembrane_system_diagram_en.svg/390px-Endomembrane_system_diagram_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Endomembrane_system_diagram_en.svg/520px-Endomembrane_system_diagram_en.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Endomembrane_system_diagram_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The endomembrane system and its components</div></div></div>
<p>Eukaryote cells include a variety of membrane-bound structures, collectively referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Endomembrane_system" title="Endomembrane system">endomembrane system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Simple compartments, called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vesicle_(biology)" title="Vesicle (biology)">vesicles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vacuole" title="Vacuole">vacuoles</a>, can form by budding off other membranes. Many cells ingest food and other materials through a process of <a href="/wiki/Endocytosis" title="Endocytosis">endocytosis</a>, where the outer membrane <a href="/wiki/Invagination" title="Invagination">invaginates</a> and then pinches off to form a vesicle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> It is probable<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> that most other membrane-bound organelles are ultimately derived from such vesicles. Alternatively some products produced by the cell can leave in a vesicle through <a href="/wiki/Exocytosis" title="Exocytosis">exocytosis</a>.
</p><p>The nucleus is surrounded by a double membrane known as the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_envelope" title="Nuclear envelope">nuclear envelope</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_pore" title="Nuclear pore">nuclear pores</a> that allow material to move in and out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheNuclearEnvelope-NCBI_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheNuclearEnvelope-NCBI-20">[20]</a></sup> Various tube- and sheet-like extensions of the nuclear membrane form the <a href="/wiki/Endoplasmic_reticulum" title="Endoplasmic reticulum">endoplasmic reticulum</a>, which is involved in protein transport and maturation. It includes the rough endoplasmic reticulum where <a href="/wiki/Ribosome" title="Ribosome">ribosomes</a> are attached to synthesize proteins, which enter the interior space or lumen. Subsequently, they generally enter vesicles, which bud off from the smooth endoplasmic reticulum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> In most eukaryotes, these protein-carrying vesicles are released and further modified in stacks of flattened vesicles (<a href="/wiki/Cisterna" title="Cisterna">cisternae</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Golgi_apparatus" title="Golgi apparatus">Golgi apparatus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Vesicles may be specialized for various purposes. For instance, <a href="/wiki/Lysosome" title="Lysosome">lysosomes</a> contain digestive <a href="/wiki/Enzyme" title="Enzyme">enzymes</a> that break down most <a href="/wiki/Biomolecule" title="Biomolecule">biomolecules</a> in the cytoplasm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peroxisome" title="Peroxisome">Peroxisomes</a> are used to break down <a href="/wiki/Peroxide" title="Peroxide">peroxide</a>, which is otherwise toxic. Many <a href="/wiki/Protozoa" title="Protozoa">protozoans</a> have contractile vacuoles, which collect and expel excess water, and <a href="/wiki/Extrusome" title="Extrusome">extrusomes</a>, which expel material used to deflect predators or capture prey. In higher plants, most of a cell's volume is taken up by a central vacuole, which mostly contains water and primarily maintains its <a href="/wiki/Osmotic_pressure" title="Osmotic pressure">osmotic pressure</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mitochondria">Mitochondria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mitochondria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mitochondrion_structure.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Mitochondrion_structure.svg/310px-Mitochondrion_structure.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Mitochondrion_structure.svg/465px-Mitochondrion_structure.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Mitochondrion_structure.svg/620px-Mitochondrion_structure.svg.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mitochondrion_structure.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Simplified structure of a mitochondrion</div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/Mitochondrion" title="Mitochondrion">Mitochondria</a> are organelles found in all but one eukaryote,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Only1_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Only1-25">[note 1]</a></sup> and are commonly referred to as "the powerhouse of the cell".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Mitochondria provide energy to the eukaryote cell by oxidising sugars or fats and releasing energy as <a href="/wiki/Adenosine_triphosphate" title="Adenosine triphosphate">ATP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> They have two surrounding <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrion#Structure" title="Mitochondrion">membranes</a>, each a <a href="/wiki/Lipid_bilayer" title="Lipid bilayer">phospholipid bi-layer</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Inner_mitochondrial_membrane" title="Inner mitochondrial membrane">inner</a> of which is folded into invaginations called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cristae" title="Cristae">cristae</a> where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aerobic_respiration" title="Aerobic respiration">aerobic respiration</a> takes place.
</p><p>The outer mitochondrial membrane is freely permeable and allows almost anything to enter into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitochondrial_intermembrane_space" title="Mitochondrial intermembrane space">intermembrane space</a> while the inner mitochondrial membrane is semi permeable so allows only some required things into the mitochondrial matrix.
</p><p>Mitochondria contain <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrial_DNA" title="Mitochondrial DNA">their own DNA</a>, which has close structural similarities to bacterial DNA, and which encodes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RRNA" title="RRNA">rRNA</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TRNA" title="TRNA">tRNA</a> genes that produce RNA which is closer in structure to bacterial RNA than to eukaryote RNA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MolecGene_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-MolecGene-28">[27]</a></sup> They are now generally held to have developed from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endosymbiosis" title="Endosymbiosis">endosymbiotic</a> prokaryotes, probably <a href="/wiki/Alphaproteobacteria" title="Alphaproteobacteria">Alphaproteobacteria</a>.
</p><p>Some eukaryotes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Metamonad" title="Metamonad">metamonads</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Giardia" title="Giardia">Giardia</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Trichomonas" title="Trichomonas">Trichomonas</a></i>, and the amoebozoan <i><a href="/wiki/Pelomyxa" title="Pelomyxa">Pelomyxa</a></i>, appear to lack mitochondria, but all have been found to contain mitochondrion-derived organelles, such as <a href="/wiki/Hydrogenosome" title="Hydrogenosome">hydrogenosomes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mitosome" title="Mitosome">mitosomes</a>, and thus have lost their mitochondria secondarily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karn_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Karn-24">[24]</a></sup> They obtain energy by enzymatic action on nutrients absorbed from the environment. The metamonad <i><a href="/wiki/Monocercomonoides" title="Monocercomonoides">Monocercomonoides</a></i> has also acquired, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lateral_gene_transfer" title="Lateral gene transfer">lateral gene transfer</a>, a cytosolic <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">sulfur</a> mobilisation system which provides the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron%E2%80%93sulfur_protein" title="Iron–sulfur protein">clusters of iron and sulfur</a> required for protein synthesis. The normal mitochondrial iron-sulfur cluster pathway has been lost secondarily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karn_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-Karn-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plastids">Plastids</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Plastids">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Plants and various groups of <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a> also have <a href="/wiki/Plastid" title="Plastid">plastids</a>. Plastids also have <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast_DNA" title="Chloroplast DNA">their own DNA</a> and are developed from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endosymbionts" title="Endosymbionts">endosymbionts</a>, in this case <a href="/wiki/Cyanobacteria" title="Cyanobacteria">cyanobacteria</a>. They usually take the form of <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">chloroplasts</a> which, like cyanobacteria, contain <a href="/wiki/Chlorophyll" title="Chlorophyll">chlorophyll</a> and produce organic compounds (such as <a href="/wiki/Glucose" title="Glucose">glucose</a>) through <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">photosynthesis</a>. Others are involved in storing food. Although plastids probably had a single origin, not all plastid-containing groups are closely related. Instead, some eukaryotes have obtained them from others through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secondary_endosymbiosis" title="Secondary endosymbiosis">secondary endosymbiosis</a> or ingestion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> The capture and sequestering of photosynthetic cells and chloroplasts occurs in many types of modern eukaryotic organisms and is known as <a href="/wiki/Kleptoplasty" title="Kleptoplasty">kleptoplasty</a>.
</p><p>Endosymbiotic origins have also been proposed for the nucleus, and for eukaryotic <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_flagella" title="Evolution of flagella">flagella</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Margulis_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Margulis-31">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cytoskeletal_structures">Cytoskeletal structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Cytoskeletal structures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cytoskeleton" title="Cytoskeleton">Cytoskeleton</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chlamydomonas_TEM_09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1438" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Chlamydomonas_TEM_09.jpg/220px-Chlamydomonas_TEM_09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Chlamydomonas_TEM_09.jpg/330px-Chlamydomonas_TEM_09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Chlamydomonas_TEM_09.jpg/440px-Chlamydomonas_TEM_09.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chlamydomonas_TEM_09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Longitudinal section through the flagellum of <i><a href="/wiki/Chlamydomonas_reinhardtii" title="Chlamydomonas reinhardtii">Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>Many eukaryotes have long slender motile cytoplasmic projections, called <a href="/wiki/Flagellum" title="Flagellum">flagella</a>, or similar structures called <a href="/wiki/Cilium" title="Cilium">cilia</a>. Flagella and cilia are sometimes referred to as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Undulipodia" title="Undulipodia">undulipodia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> and are variously involved in movement, feeding, and sensation. They are composed mainly of <a href="/wiki/Tubulin" title="Tubulin">tubulin</a>. These are entirely distinct from prokaryotic flagellae. They are supported by a bundle of microtubules arising from a <a href="/wiki/Centriole" title="Centriole">centriole</a>, characteristically arranged as nine doublets surrounding two singlets. Flagella also may have hairs, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mastigonemes" title="Mastigonemes">mastigonemes</a>, and scales connecting membranes and internal rods. Their interior is continuous with the cell's <a href="/wiki/Cytoplasm" title="Cytoplasm">cytoplasm</a>.
</p><p>Microfilamental structures composed of <a href="/wiki/Actin" title="Actin">actin</a> and actin binding proteins, e.g., α-<a href="/wiki/Actinin" title="Actinin">actinin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fimbrin" title="Fimbrin">fimbrin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filamin" title="Filamin">filamin</a> are present in submembranous cortical layers and bundles, as well. <a href="/wiki/Motor_protein" title="Motor protein">Motor proteins</a> of microtubules, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Dynein" title="Dynein">dynein</a> or <a href="/wiki/Kinesin" title="Kinesin">kinesin</a> and actin, e.g., <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myosins" title="Myosins">myosins</a> provide dynamic character of the network.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centrioles" title="Centrioles">Centrioles</a> are often present even in cells and groups that do not have flagella, but <a href="/wiki/Conifer" title="Conifer">conifers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a> have neither. They generally occur in groups that give rise to various microtubular roots. These form a primary component of the cytoskeletal structure, and are often assembled over the course of several cell divisions, with one flagellum retained from the parent and the other derived from it. Centrioles produce the spindle during nuclear division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>The significance of cytoskeletal structures is underlined in the determination of shape of the cells, as well as their being essential components of migratory responses like <a href="/wiki/Chemotaxis" title="Chemotaxis">chemotaxis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chemokinesis" title="Chemokinesis">chemokinesis</a>. Some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protists" title="Protists">protists</a> have various other microtubule-supported organelles. These include the <a href="/wiki/Radiolaria" title="Radiolaria">radiolaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heliozoa" title="Heliozoa">heliozoa</a>, which produce <a href="/wiki/Pseudopodia#Morphology" title="Pseudopodia">axopodia</a> used in flotation or to capture prey, and the <a href="/wiki/Haptophyte" title="Haptophyte">haptophytes</a>, which have a peculiar flagellum-like organelle called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haptonema" title="Haptonema">haptonema</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cell_wall">Cell wall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Cell wall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cell_wall" title="Cell wall">Cell wall</a></div>
<p>The cells of plants and algae, fungi and most <a href="/wiki/Chromalveolata" title="Chromalveolata">chromalveolates</a> have a cell wall, a layer outside the <a href="/wiki/Cell_membrane" title="Cell membrane">cell membrane</a>, providing the cell with structural support, protection, and a filtering mechanism. The cell wall also prevents over-expansion when water enters the cell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Howland_2000_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Howland_2000-34">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>The major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polysaccharides" title="Polysaccharides">polysaccharides</a> making up the primary cell wall of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_plants" title="Land plants">land plants</a> are <a href="/wiki/Cellulose" title="Cellulose">cellulose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hemicellulose" title="Hemicellulose">hemicellulose</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pectin" title="Pectin">pectin</a>. The cellulose <a href="/wiki/Microfibril" title="Microfibril">microfibrils</a> are linked via hemicellulosic tethers to form the cellulose-hemicellulose network, which is embedded in the pectin matrix. The most common hemicellulose in the primary cell wall is <a href="/wiki/Xyloglucan" title="Xyloglucan">xyloglucan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fry1989_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fry1989-35">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Differences_among_eukaryotic_cells">Differences among eukaryotic cells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Differences among eukaryotic cells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are many different types of eukaryotic cells, though animals and plants are the most familiar eukaryotes, and thus provide an excellent starting point for understanding eukaryotic structure. Fungi and many protists have some substantial differences, however.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_cell">Animal cell</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Animal cell">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Animal_cell_structure_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="484" data-file-width="724" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Animal_cell_structure_en.svg/310px-Animal_cell_structure_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Animal_cell_structure_en.svg/465px-Animal_cell_structure_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Animal_cell_structure_en.svg/620px-Animal_cell_structure_en.svg.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Animal_cell_structure_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Structure of a typical animal cell</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plant_cell_structure-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="475" data-file-width="649" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Plant_cell_structure-en.svg/310px-Plant_cell_structure-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Plant_cell_structure-en.svg/465px-Plant_cell_structure-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Plant_cell_structure-en.svg/620px-Plant_cell_structure-en.svg.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plant_cell_structure-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Structure of a typical <a href="/wiki/Plant_cell" title="Plant cell">plant cell</a></div></div></div>
<p>All animals are eukaryotic. Animal cells are distinct from those of other eukaryotes, most notably <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plant_cells" title="Plant cells">plants</a>, as they lack <a href="/wiki/Cell_wall" title="Cell wall">cell walls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">chloroplasts</a> and have smaller <a href="/wiki/Vacuole" title="Vacuole">vacuoles</a>. Due to the lack of a <a href="/wiki/Cell_wall" title="Cell wall">cell wall</a>, animal cells can transform into a variety of shapes. A <a href="/wiki/Phagocyte" title="Phagocyte">phagocytic</a> cell can even engulf other structures.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plant_cell">Plant cell</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Plant cell">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plant_cell" title="Plant cell">Plant cell</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Plant_cell" title="Plant cell">Plant cells</a> are quite different from the cells of the other eukaryotic organisms. Their distinctive features are:
</p>
<ul><li>A large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_vacuole" title="Central vacuole">central vacuole</a> (enclosed by a membrane, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonoplast" title="Tonoplast">tonoplast</a>), which maintains the cell's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turgor" title="Turgor">turgor</a> and controls movement of <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">molecules</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Cytosol" title="Cytosol">cytosol</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plant_sap" title="Plant sap">sap</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raven1987_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raven1987-36">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li>A primary <a href="/wiki/Cell_wall" title="Cell wall">cell wall</a> containing <a href="/wiki/Cellulose" title="Cellulose">cellulose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hemicellulose" title="Hemicellulose">hemicellulose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pectin" title="Pectin">pectin</a>, deposited by the <a href="/wiki/Protoplast" title="Protoplast">protoplast</a> on the outside of the <a href="/wiki/Cell_membrane" title="Cell membrane">cell membrane</a>; this contrasts with the cell walls of <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a>, which contain <a href="/wiki/Chitin" title="Chitin">chitin</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cell_envelope" title="Cell envelope">cell envelopes</a> of prokaryotes, in which <a href="/wiki/Peptidoglycan" title="Peptidoglycan">peptidoglycans</a> are the main structural molecules</li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plasmodesmata" title="Plasmodesmata">plasmodesmata</a>, pores in the cell wall that link adjacent cells and allow plant cells to communicate with adjacent cells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oparka_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oparka-37">[36]</a></sup> Animals have a different but functionally analogous system of <a href="/wiki/Gap_junction" title="Gap junction">gap junctions</a> between adjacent cells.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Plastid" title="Plastid">Plastids</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">chloroplasts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organelle" title="Organelle">organelles</a> that contain <a href="/wiki/Chlorophyll" title="Chlorophyll">chlorophyll</a>, the pigment that gives <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a> their green color and allows them to perform <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">photosynthesis</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bryophyte" title="Bryophyte">Bryophytes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pteridophyte" title="Pteridophyte">seedless vascular plants</a> only have flagellae and centrioles in the sperm cells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raven_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raven-38">[37]</a></sup> Sperm of <a href="/wiki/Cycad" title="Cycad">cycads</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ginkgo" title="Ginkgo">Ginkgo</a></i> are large, complex cells that swim with hundreds to thousands of flagellae.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Silflow_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Silflow-39">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinophyta" title="Pinophyta">Conifers</a> (Pinophyta) and <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a> (Angiospermae) lack the <a href="/wiki/Flagellum" title="Flagellum">flagellae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Centriole" title="Centriole">centrioles</a> that are present in animal cells.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fungal_cell">Fungal cell</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Fungal cell">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HYPHAE.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="721" data-file-width="1364" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/HYPHAE.png/310px-HYPHAE.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/HYPHAE.png/465px-HYPHAE.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/HYPHAE.png/620px-HYPHAE.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HYPHAE.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fungal Hyphae cells: 1 – hyphal wall, 2 – septum, 3 – mitochondrion, 4 – vacuole, 5 – <a href="/wiki/Ergosterol" title="Ergosterol">ergosterol</a> crystal, 6 – ribosome, 7 – nucleus, 8 – endoplasmic reticulum, 9 – lipid body, 10 – plasma membrane, 11 – <a href="/wiki/Spitzenk%C3%B6rper" title="Spitzenkörper">spitzenkörper</a>, 12 – Golgi apparatus</div></div></div>
<p>The cells of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fungi" title="Fungi">fungi</a> are similar to animal cells, with the following exceptions:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>A cell wall that contains <a href="/wiki/Chitin" title="Chitin">chitin</a></li>
<li>Less compartmentation between cells; the <a href="/wiki/Hypha" title="Hypha">hyphae</a> of higher fungi have porous partitions called <a href="/wiki/Septum" title="Septum">septa</a>, which allow the passage of cytoplasm, organelles, and, sometimes, nuclei; so each organism is essentially a giant <a href="/wiki/Multinucleate" title="Multinucleate">multinucleate</a> supercell – these fungi are described as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coenocytic" title="Coenocytic">coenocytic</a>. Primitive fungi have few or no septa.</li>
<li>Only the most primitive fungi, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chytrid" title="Chytrid">chytrids</a>, have flagella.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_eukaryotic_cells">Other eukaryotic cells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other eukaryotic cells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some groups of eukaryotes have unique organelles, such as the cyanelles (unusual plastids) of the <a href="/wiki/Glaucophyte" title="Glaucophyte">glaucophytes</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keeling_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-keeling-41">[40]</a></sup> the haptonema of the <a href="/wiki/Haptophyte" title="Haptophyte">haptophytes</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Ejectosome" title="Ejectosome">ejectosomes</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Cryptomonad" title="Cryptomonad">cryptomonads</a>. Other structures, such as <a href="/wiki/Pseudopodia" title="Pseudopodia">pseudopodia</a>, are found in various eukaryote groups in different forms, such as the lobose <a href="/wiki/Amoebozoa" title="Amoebozoa">amoebozoans</a> or the reticulose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foraminiferan" title="Foraminiferan">foraminiferans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reproduction">Reproduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Reproduction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evolsex-dia1a.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="389" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Evolsex-dia1a.png/310px-Evolsex-dia1a.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Evolsex-dia1a.png/465px-Evolsex-dia1a.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Evolsex-dia1a.png/620px-Evolsex-dia1a.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evolsex-dia1a.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This diagram illustrates the <i>twofold cost of sex</i>. If each individual were to contribute the same number of offspring (two), <i>(a)</i> the sexual population remains the same size each generation, where the <i>(b)</i> asexual population doubles in size each generation.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cell_division" title="Cell division">Cell division</a> generally takes place <a href="/wiki/Asexual_reproduction" title="Asexual reproduction">asexually</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mitosis" title="Mitosis">mitosis</a>, a process that allows each daughter nucleus to receive one copy of each <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosome</a>. Most eukaryotes also have a life cycle that involves <a href="/wiki/Sexual_reproduction" title="Sexual reproduction">sexual reproduction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alternation_of_generations" title="Alternation of generations">alternating</a> between a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haploid" title="Haploid">haploid</a> phase, where only one copy of each chromosome is present in each cell and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diploid" title="Diploid">diploid</a> phase, wherein two copies of each chromosome are present in each cell. The diploid phase is formed by fusion of two haploid gametes to form a zygote, which may divide by mitosis or undergo chromosome reduction by <a href="/wiki/Meiosis" title="Meiosis">meiosis</a>. There is considerable variation in this pattern. Animals have no multicellular haploid phase, but each plant generation can consist of haploid and diploid multicellular phases.
</p><p>Eukaryotes have a smaller surface area to volume ratio than prokaryotes, and thus have lower metabolic rates and longer generation times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lane2011_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lane2011-43">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_sexual_reproduction" title="Evolution of sexual reproduction">evolution of sexual reproduction</a> may be a primordial and fundamental characteristic of eukaryotes. Based on a phylogenetic analysis, Dacks and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_J._Roger" title="Andrew J. Roger">Roger</a> proposed that facultative sex was present in the common ancestor of all eukaryotes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> A core set of genes that function in meiosis is present in both <i><a href="/wiki/Trichomonas_vaginalis" title="Trichomonas vaginalis">Trichomonas vaginalis</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giardia_intestinalis" title="Giardia intestinalis">Giardia intestinalis</a></i>, two organisms previously thought to be asexual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramesh_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ramesh-45">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malik_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malik-46">[45]</a></sup> Since these two species are descendants of lineages that diverged early from the eukaryotic evolutionary tree, it was inferred that core meiotic genes, and hence sex, were likely present in a common ancestor of all eukaryotes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramesh_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ramesh-45">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malik_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Malik-46">[45]</a></sup> Eukaryotic species once thought to be asexual, such as parasitic protozoa of the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Leishmania" title="Leishmania">Leishmania</a></i>, have been shown to have a sexual cycle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Also, evidence now indicates that amoebae, previously regarded as asexual, are anciently sexual and that the majority of present-day asexual groups likely arose recently and independently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Classification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="extiw" href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Eukaryota" title="wikispecies:Eukaryota">wikispecies:Eukaryota</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1533" data-file-width="1530" decoding="async" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png/310px-Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png/465px-Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png/620px-Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Phylogenetic and symbiogenetic tree of living organisms, showing a view of the origins of eukaryotes and prokaryotes</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eukaryote_Phylogeny.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="876" data-file-width="1569" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Eukaryote_Phylogeny.png/220px-Eukaryote_Phylogeny.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Eukaryote_Phylogeny.png/330px-Eukaryote_Phylogeny.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Eukaryote_Phylogeny.png/440px-Eukaryote_Phylogeny.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eukaryote_Phylogeny.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One hypothesis of eukaryotic relationships – the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opisthokonta" title="Opisthokonta">Opisthokonta</a> group includes both animals (Metazoa) and fungi, plants (Plantae) are placed in <a href="/wiki/Archaeplastida" title="Archaeplastida">Archaeplastida</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eukaryote_species_pie_tree.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="1117" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Eukaryote_species_pie_tree.png/310px-Eukaryote_species_pie_tree.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Eukaryote_species_pie_tree.png/465px-Eukaryote_species_pie_tree.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Eukaryote_species_pie_tree.png/620px-Eukaryote_species_pie_tree.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eukaryote_species_pie_tree.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A pie chart of described eukaryote species (except for Excavata), together with a tree showing possible relationships between the groups</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">antiquity</a>, the two lineages of <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a> were recognized. They were given the <a href="/wiki/Taxonomic_rank" title="Taxonomic rank">taxonomic rank</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)" title="Kingdom (biology)">Kingdom</a> by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus" title="Carl Linnaeus">Linnaeus</a>. Though he included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fungi" title="Fungi">fungi</a> with plants with some reservations, it was later realized that they are quite distinct and warrant a separate kingdom, the composition of which was not entirely clear until the 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moore1980_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moore1980-49">[48]</a></sup> The various single-cell eukaryotes were originally placed with plants or animals when they became known. In 1818, the German biologist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georg_A._Goldfuss" title="Georg A. Goldfuss">Georg A. Goldfuss</a> coined the word <i><a href="/wiki/Protozoa" title="Protozoa">protozoa</a></i> to refer to organisms such as <a href="/wiki/Ciliate" title="Ciliate">ciliates</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> and this group was expanded until it encompassed all single-celled eukaryotes, and given their own kingdom, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protista" title="Protista">Protista</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Haeckel" title="Ernst Haeckel">Ernst Haeckel</a> in 1866.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scamardella1999_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scamardella1999-51">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1989_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1989-52">[51]</a></sup> The eukaryotes thus came to be composed of four kingdoms:
</p>
<ul><li>Kingdom <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protista" title="Protista">Protista</a></li>
<li>Kingdom <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantae" title="Plantae">Plantae</a></li>
<li>Kingdom <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fungi" title="Fungi">Fungi</a></li>
<li>Kingdom <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animalia" title="Animalia">Animalia</a></li></ul>
<p>The protists were understood to be "primitive forms", and thus an <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_grade" title="Evolutionary grade">evolutionary grade</a>, united by their primitive unicellular nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1989_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1989-52">[51]</a></sup> The disentanglement of the deep splits in the <a href="/wiki/Tree_of_life_(biology)" title="Tree of life (biology)">tree of life</a> only really started with <a href="/wiki/Nucleic_acid_sequence" title="Nucleic acid sequence">DNA sequencing</a>, leading to a system of <a href="/wiki/Domain_(biology)" title="Domain (biology)">domains</a> rather than kingdoms as top level rank being put forward by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Woese" title="Carl Woese">Carl Woese</a>, uniting all the eukaryote kingdoms under the eukaryote domain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-53">[52]</a></sup> At the same time, work on the protist tree intensified, and is still actively going on today. Several alternative classifications have been forwarded, though there is no consensus in the field.
</p><p>Eukaryotes are a clade usually assessed to be sister to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heimdallarchaeota" title="Heimdallarchaeota">Heimdallarchaeota</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Asgard_(archaea)" title="Asgard (archaea)">Asgard</a> grouping in the <a href="/wiki/Archaea" title="Archaea">Archaea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpangSaw2015_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-SpangSaw2015-54">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zaremba-NiedzwiedzkaCaceres2017_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zaremba-NiedzwiedzkaCaceres2017-55">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liu_2018_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Liu_2018-56">[55]</a></sup> In one proposed system<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (August 2022)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup>, the basal groupings are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opimoda" title="Opimoda">Opimoda</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diphoda" title="Diphoda">Diphoda</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discoba" title="Discoba">Discoba</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Loukozoa" title="Loukozoa">Loukozoa</a>. The Eukaryote root is usually assessed to be near or even in Discoba<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)#International_Society_of_Protistologists_Classification_2005" title="Kingdom (biology)">classification produced in 2005 for the International Society of Protistologists</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> which reflected the consensus of the time, divided the eukaryotes into six supposedly monophyletic 'supergroups'. However, in the same year (2005), doubts were expressed as to whether some of these supergroups were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monophyletic" title="Monophyletic">monophyletic</a>, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Chromalveolata" title="Chromalveolata">Chromalveolata</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> and a review in 2006 noted the lack of evidence for several of the supposed six supergroups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parfrey_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-parfrey-59">[58]</a></sup> A revised classification in 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adl2012_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adl2012-60">[59]</a></sup> recognizes five supergroups.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Archaeplastida" title="Archaeplastida">Archaeplastida</a><br/>(or Primoplantae)</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Embryophyte" title="Embryophyte">Land plants</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_alga" title="Green alga">green algae</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_alga" title="Red alga">red algae</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Glaucophyte" title="Glaucophyte">glaucophytes</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/SAR_supergroup" title="SAR supergroup">SAR supergroup</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Heterokont" title="Heterokont">Stramenopiles</a> (<a href="/wiki/Brown_algae" title="Brown algae">brown algae</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diatoms" title="Diatoms">diatoms</a>, etc.),<br/><a href="/wiki/Alveolate" title="Alveolate">Alveolata</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rhizaria" title="Rhizaria">Rhizaria</a> (<a href="/wiki/Foraminifera" title="Foraminifera">Foraminifera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radiolaria" title="Radiolaria">Radiolaria</a>,<br/>and various other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amoeboid" title="Amoeboid">amoeboid</a> protozoa)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Excavata" title="Excavata">Excavata</a></td>
<td>Various <a href="/wiki/Flagellate" title="Flagellate">flagellate</a> protozoa
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Amoebozoa" title="Amoebozoa">Amoebozoa</a></td>
<td>Most lobose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amoeboid" title="Amoeboid">amoeboids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slime_mold" title="Slime mold">slime molds</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opisthokonta" title="Opisthokonta">Opisthokonta</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">Animals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Choanoflagellate" title="Choanoflagellate">choanoflagellates</a>, etc.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There are also smaller groups of eukaryotes whose position is uncertain or seems to fall outside the major groups<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burki2014_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-burki2014-61">[60]</a></sup> – in particular, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haptophyta" title="Haptophyta">Haptophyta</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cryptophyta" title="Cryptophyta">Cryptophyta</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centrohelida" title="Centrohelida">Centrohelida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telonemia" title="Telonemia">Telonemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Picozoa" title="Picozoa">Picozoa</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZhaoBurkBratKeel12_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-ZhaoBurkBratKeel12-62">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Apusomonadida" title="Apusomonadida">Apusomonadida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancyromonadida" title="Ancyromonadida">Ancyromonadida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breviata" title="Breviata">Breviatea</a>, and the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Collodictyon" title="Collodictyon">Collodictyon</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Romari2004_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Romari2004-63">[62]</a></sup> Overall, it seems that, although progress has been made, there are still very significant uncertainties in the evolutionary history and classification of eukaryotes. As <a href="/wiki/Andrew_J._Roger" title="Andrew J. Roger">Roger</a> &amp; Simpson said in 2009 "with the current pace of change in our understanding of the eukaryote tree of life, we should proceed with caution."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> Newly identified protists, purported to represent novel, deep-branching lineages, continue to be described well into the 21st century; recent examples including <i><a href="/wiki/Rhodelphis" title="Rhodelphis">Rhodelphis</a></i>, putative sister group to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodophyta" title="Rhodophyta">Rhodophyta</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Anaeramoeba" title="Anaeramoeba">Anaeramoeba</a></i>, anaerobic amoebaflagellates of uncertain placement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BurkiRoger2020_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-BurkiRoger2020-65">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phylogeny">Phylogeny</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Phylogeny">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RRNA" title="RRNA">rRNA</a> trees constructed during the 1980s and 1990s left most eukaryotes in an unresolved "crown" group (not technically a true <a href="/wiki/Crown_group" title="Crown group">crown</a>), which was usually divided by the form of the mitochondrial cristae; see <a href="/wiki/Crown_eukaryotes" title="Crown eukaryotes">crown eukaryotes</a>. The few groups that lack <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitochondria" title="Mitochondria">mitochondria</a> branched separately, and so the absence was believed to be primitive; but this is now considered an artifact of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long-branch_attraction" title="Long-branch attraction">long-branch attraction</a>, and they are known to have lost them secondarily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>It has been estimated that there may be 75 distinct lineages of eukaryotes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jagus2012_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jagus2012-68">[67]</a></sup> Most of these lineages are protists.
</p><p>The known eukaryote genome sizes vary from 8.2 megabases (Mb) in <i><a href="/wiki/Babesia_bovis" title="Babesia bovis">Babesia bovis</a></i> to 112,000–220,050 Mb in the dinoflagellate <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Prorocentrum_micans&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Prorocentrum micans (page does not exist)">Prorocentrum micans</a></i>, showing that the genome of the ancestral eukaryote has undergone considerable variation during its evolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jagus2012_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jagus2012-68">[67]</a></sup> The last common ancestor of all eukaryotes is believed to have been a phagotrophic protist with a nucleus, at least one <a href="/wiki/Centriole" title="Centriole">centriole</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cilium" title="Cilium">cilium</a>, facultatively aerobic mitochondria, sex (<a href="/wiki/Meiosis" title="Meiosis">meiosis</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syngamy" title="Syngamy">syngamy</a>), a dormant <a href="/wiki/Cyst" title="Cyst">cyst</a> with a cell wall of <a href="/wiki/Chitin" title="Chitin">chitin</a> and/or <a href="/wiki/Cellulose" title="Cellulose">cellulose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peroxisome" title="Peroxisome">peroxisomes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jagus2012_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jagus2012-68">[67]</a></sup> Later endosymbiosis led to the spread of plastids in some lineages.
</p><p>Although there is still considerable uncertainty in global eukaryote phylogeny, particularly regarding the position of the root, a rough consensus has started to emerge from the phylogenomic studies of the past two decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burki2014_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-burki2014-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_2018_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_2018-72">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karn_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-Karn-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BurkiRoger2020_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-BurkiRoger2020-65">[64]</a></sup> The majority of eukaryotes can be placed in one of two large clades dubbed <a href="/wiki/Amorphea" title="Amorphea">Amorphea</a> (similar in composition to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unikont" title="Unikont">unikont</a> hypothesis) and the <a href="/wiki/Diaphoretickes" title="Diaphoretickes">Diaphoretickes</a>, which includes plants and most algal lineages. A third major grouping, the <a href="/wiki/Excavata" title="Excavata">Excavata</a>, has been abandoned as a formal group in the most recent classification of the International Society of Protistologists due to growing uncertainty as to whether its constituent groups belong together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdlBass2019_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-AdlBass2019-75">[74]</a></sup> The proposed phylogeny below includes only one group of excavates (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discoba" title="Discoba">Discoba</a>), and incorporates the recent proposal that <a href="/wiki/Picozoa" title="Picozoa">picozoans</a> are close relatives of rhodophytes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SchönZlatogursky2021_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-SchönZlatogursky2021-76">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r984819063">.mw-parser-output table.clade{border-spacing:0;margin:0;font-size:100%;line-height:100%;border-collapse:separate;width:auto}.mw-parser-output table.clade table.clade{width:100%;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label{width:0.7em;padding:0 0.15em;vertical-align:bottom;text-align:center;border-left:1px solid;border-bottom:1px solid;white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-fixed-width{overflow:hidden;text-overflow:ellipsis}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-fixed-width:hover{overflow:visible}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label.first{border-left:none;border-right:none}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label.reverse{border-left:none;border-right:1px solid}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel{padding:0 0.15em;vertical-align:top;text-align:center;border-left:1px solid;white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel:hover{overflow:visible}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel.last{border-left:none;border-right:none}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel.reverse{border-left:none;border-right:1px solid}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-bar{vertical-align:middle;text-align:left;padding:0 0.5em;position:relative}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-bar.reverse{text-align:right;position:relative}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leaf{border:0;padding:0;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leafR{border:0;padding:0;text-align:right}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leaf.reverse{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output table.clade:hover span.linkA{background-color:yellow}.mw-parser-output table.clade:hover span.linkB{background-color:green}</style>

<td class="clade-label first"> 
</td>
<td class="clade-leaf" rowspan="2">
<p><a href="/wiki/Holomycota" title="Holomycota">Holomycota</a> (inc. fungi) <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asco1013.jpg"><img alt="Asco1013.jpg" data-file-height="941" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="47" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Asco1013.jpg/60px-Asco1013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Asco1013.jpg/90px-Asco1013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Asco1013.jpg/120px-Asco1013.jpg 2x" width="60"/></a>

<td class="clade-label"> 
</td>
<td class="clade-leaf" rowspan="2">
<p><a href="/wiki/Holozoa" title="Holozoa">Holozoa</a> (inc. animals) <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Comb_jelly.jpg"><img alt="Comb jelly.jpg" data-file-height="2177" data-file-width="1588" decoding="async" height="62" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Comb_jelly.jpg/45px-Comb_jelly.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Comb_jelly.jpg/68px-Comb_jelly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Comb_jelly.jpg/90px-Comb_jelly.jpg 2x" width="45"/></a>
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel last"> 
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel last"> 
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel last"> 
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel last"> 
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel last" style="font-size:80%; line-height:80%"> 
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In some analyses, the <a href="/wiki/Hacrobia" title="Hacrobia">Hacrobia</a> group (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haptophyta" title="Haptophyta">Haptophyta</a> + <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cryptophyta" title="Cryptophyta">Cryptophyta</a>) is placed next to <a href="/wiki/Archaeplastida" title="Archaeplastida">Archaeplastida</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burki2007_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burki2007-77">[76]</a></sup> but in others it is nested inside the Archaeplastida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KimGraham2008_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-KimGraham2008-78">[77]</a></sup> However, several recent studies have concluded that Haptophyta and Cryptophyta do not form a monophyletic group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BaurBrinPeteRodr10_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-BaurBrinPeteRodr10-79">[78]</a></sup> The former could be a sister group to the <a href="/wiki/SAR_supergroup" title="SAR supergroup">SAR group</a>, the latter cluster with the <a href="/wiki/Archaeplastida" title="Archaeplastida">Archaeplastida</a> (plants in the broad sense).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burki2012_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burki2012-80">[79]</a></sup>
</p><p>The division of the eukaryotes into two primary clades, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bikonts" title="Bikonts">bikonts</a> (<a href="/wiki/Archaeplastida" title="Archaeplastida">Archaeplastida</a> + <a href="/wiki/SAR_supergroup" title="SAR supergroup">SAR</a> + <a href="/wiki/Excavata" title="Excavata">Excavata</a>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unikonts" title="Unikonts">unikonts</a> (<a href="/wiki/Amoebozoa" title="Amoebozoa">Amoebozoa</a> + <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opisthokonta" title="Opisthokonta">Opisthokonta</a>), derived from an ancestral biflagellar organism and an ancestral uniflagellar organism, respectively, had been suggested earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KimGraham2008_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-KimGraham2008-78">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CavalierSmith2006_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-CavalierSmith2006-81">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid16829542_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16829542-82">[81]</a></sup> A 2012 study produced a somewhat similar division, although noting that the terms "unikonts" and "bikonts" were not used in the original sense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZhaoBurkBratKeel12_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-ZhaoBurkBratKeel12-62">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>A highly converged and congruent set of trees appears in Derelle et al. (2015), Ren et al. (2016), Yang et al. (2017) and Cavalier-Smith (2015) including the supplementary information, resulting in a more conservative and consolidated tree. It is combined with some results from Cavalier-Smith for the basal Opimoda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavalier-Smith_2018_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith_2018-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_2018_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_2018-72">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> The main remaining controversies are the root, and the exact positioning of the Rhodophyta and the <a href="/wiki/Bikont" title="Bikont">bikonts</a> Rhizaria, Haptista, Cryptista, Picozoa and Telonemia, many of which may be endosymbiotic eukaryote-eukaryote hybrids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-López-García_2017_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-López-García_2017-89">[88]</a></sup> Archaeplastida acquired <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">chloroplasts</a> probably by endosymbiosis of a prokaryotic ancestor related to a currently extant <a href="/wiki/Cyanobacteria" title="Cyanobacteria">cyanobacterium</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gloeomargarita_lithophora" title="Gloeomargarita lithophora">Gloeomargarita lithophora</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-López-García_2017_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-López-García_2017-89">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r984819063" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
<table class="clade" style="font-size:80%; line-height:80%">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="clade-label first">Eukaryotes
</td>
<td class="clade-leaf" rowspan="2">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r984819063" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
<table class="clade">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="clade-label first"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diphoda" title="Diphoda">Diphoda</a>

</td>
<td class="clade-leaf" rowspan="2">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r984819063" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
<table class="clade">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="clade-label first"> 
</td>
<td class="clade-leaf" rowspan="2">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r984819063" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
<table class="clade">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="clade-label first"><a href="/wiki/Archaeplastida" title="Archaeplastida">Archaeplastida</a>
</td>
<td class="clade-leaf" rowspan="2">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r984819063" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>

</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel"> 
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-label">

<h4><span id="Cavalier-Smith.27s_tree"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cavalier-Smith's_tree">Cavalier-Smith's tree</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eukaryote&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cavalier-Smith's tree">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cavalier-Smith" title="Thomas Cavalier-Smith">Thomas Cavalier-Smith</a> 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavalier-Smith2010b_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith2010b-92">[91]</a></sup> 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavalier-Smith2013_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith2013-93">[92]</a></sup> 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cavalier2014_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-cavalier2014-94">[93]</a></sup> 2017<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavalier-Smith_2018_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith_2018-84">[83]</a></sup> and 2018<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> places the eukaryotic tree's root between <a href="/wiki/Excavata" title="Excavata">Excavata</a> (with ventral feeding groove supported by a microtubular root) and the grooveless <a href="/wiki/Euglenozoa" title="Euglenozoa">Euglenozoa</a>, and monophyletic Chromista, correlated to a single endosymbiotic event of capturing a red-algae. He et al.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> specifically supports rooting the eukaryotic tree between a monophyletic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discoba" title="Discoba">Discoba</a> (<a href="/wiki/Discicristata" title="Discicristata">Discicristata</a> + <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jakobidae" title="Jakobidae">Jakobida</a>) and an <a href="/wiki/Amorphea" title="Amorphea">Amorphea</a>-<a href="/wiki/Diaphoretickes" title="Diaphoretickes">Diaphoretickes</a> clade.
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r984819063" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
